\section*{CEMAC, Communauté économique et monétaire d'Afrique centrale, rei080} 

treaty list last updated 201211 by gary goertz 
coding finished 20131115

Communauté économique et monétaire d'Afrique centrale (CEMAC) created in 1994
Central Africa Economic and Monetary Community (CAEMC) 
Union douanière et économique de l'Afrique centrale (UDEAC) created in 1991

http://www.cemac.int/
for some treaties:
http://www.cemac.int/TextesOfficiels/actes.htm
http://www.izf.net/upload/Documentation/JournalOfficiel/Index%20cemac.htm
these sites do not have stuff from the 1960s

we consider that it starts in 1964

Africa: Cameroon, Central African Rep, Chad, Congo Brazzaville, Equatorial Guinea, Gabon

Brazzaville (Congo Brazzaville), 19641208 on signature of Brazzaville Treaty by Heads of State of Cameroon, Central African Republic, Chad, Congo and Gabon, which entered into force 1 Jan 1966, following protocol signed 11 Feb 1964, Fort-Lamy. Replaced Equatorial Customs Union -- Union douanière équatoriale (UDE), set up 23 June 1959, by Conference of Heads of State of Equatorial Africa, the Heads of State of the 4 previous colonies comprising Afrique équatoriale française (AEF) - Central African Republic, Chad, Congo and Gabon - which had become independent in 1960; and the subsequent Union douanière équatoriale-Cameroun (UDE-Cameroun) set up on signature of a convention on economic relations and customs between UDE and the Cameroon, 23 June 1961, Bangui (Central African Rep). Under the terms of the Brazzaville Treaty, UDE was also succeeded by UDEAC Solidarity Fund -- Fonds de solidarité de l'UDEAC. Central African Republic and Chad withdrew, Apr 1968, to form, together with Congo-Kinshasa, the short-lived Union des Etats de l'Afrique centrale. Central African Republic rejoined UDEAC in Dec 1968. Equatorial Guinea joined UDEAC in 1983 and Chad rejoined in 1984, ratified at meeting of Heads of State, 17-19 Dec 1987, Brazzaville. Council of Heads of State, Dec 1991, set up a study with a view to: relaunching a policy of economic and social integration; consolidating members' experience in economic and monetary cooperation through reinforcement of common currency; ordering macro-economic policies; setting up a regional legal framework for investment and growth; achieving a single market; setting up common sectoral policies. This resulted in the setting up of Communauté économique et monétaire d'Afrique centrale, 16 Mar 1994, replacing UDEAC and at the same time absorbing Union monétaire de l'Afrique centrale. Union économique de l'Afrique centrale, which is a CEMAC institution, has gradually taken over the activities of UDEAC. This transition was formalized in a agreement signed by the Council on 5 Feb 1997, Libreville, effective 1 Jan 1998

Ndjamena (Chad), 19940316 on signature of a treaty by heads of member states, following a study proposed by the Council of Heads of State of Union douanière et économique de l'Afrique centrale, Dec 1991. Retains the principles inherent in the creation of UDEAC and of Union monétaire de l'Afrique centrale (UMAC), set up 22 Nov 1972, Brazzaville (Congo Brazzaville), by 5 Central African states and by Government of France and of which Equatorial Guinea became a member as from 1 Jan 1985. UMAC is also referred to in English as Central African Monetary System and Central African Monetary Area (CAMA), and in French as Zone monétaire centrafricaine. UMAC was absorbed into CEMAC, which took over the activities of UDEAC through a transition formalized in an agreement signed by the UDEAC Council on 5 Feb 1997, Libreville (Gabon), effective 1 Jan 1998. CEMAC comes within the framework of Pays africains de la Zone franc, having the common currency - CFA franc - of the Communauté financière africaine. All relevant treaties and conventions are deposited in the state of Chad

NOTE: there are quite a few "reglement" and "decision". we only include "traite" "convention" and "acte" for coding as international treaties. However, some "actes" are excluded as minor and more like decisions. it seems over time that "acte" no longer is used and terms like "directive" replace it.

\section*{Common Market for Eastern & Southern Africa (COMESA), rei120}

official web site: 
http://www.comesa.int/

treaty coding considered done 201305

"gazettes" which are mostly "decisions" checked for treaties, see reidevon gazettes subfolder, website is missing gazettes for 2002-2008, it appears that it was not published during this period, see also summit communiques in reidevon

COMESA formed in December 1994, replacing a Preferential Trade Area which had existed since 1981 http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Common_Market_for_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa

19811221 Preferential Trade Area for Eastern and Southern Africa signed Lusaka on 21st December 1981. The Treaty came into force on 30th September 1982 after it had been ratified by more than seven signatory states as provided for in Article 50 of the Treaty. "Preferential Trade Area for Eastern and Southern Africa" rei120.10 rei120.10tt2.webarchive describes the original treaty in some detail and PTA institutions-organizations, copy of treaty not yet found rei120.10cs.txt

19849999 The Clearing House: The PTA Clearing House was set up in 1984 under the Reserve Bank of Zimbabwe. In January 1992 the Clearing House was formally established under its own charter with its own secretariat, headquartered in Harare, and run by an executive secretary. The objective of the Clearing House is to promote cooperation in the settlement of payments for intraPTA trade. The Clearing House operates a payments scheme which allows for settlement of day-to-day payments in member state's currencies. rei120.19 rei120.19cs.txt

19851106 "CHARTER OF THE EASTERN AND SOUTHERN AFRICAN TRADE AND DEVELOPMENT BANK" The Eastern and Southern African Trade and Development Bank, commonly known as the PTA Bank, was established on 6th November, 1985 pursuant to the provisions of Chapter 9 of the Treaty (1981) establishing the Preferential Trade Area for the Eastern and Southern African States (PTA) which was later transformed into the Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa (COMESA). http://www.ptabank.org/index.php?page=Our-Background rei120.11 rei120.11tt1.pdf rei120.11cs.txt

19889999 In 1988 the Articles of Association were signed and the inaugural meeting took place in 1989 in Arusha, Tanzania. In 1994 the Association was renamed the COMESA Bankers' Association. rei120.21 rei120.21cs.txt rei120.21tt1.pdf rei120.21tt2.txt (2001 version, 4th revision)

19901123 The Leather and Leather Products Institute (LLPI): The LLPI was established in Addis Ababa in November 1993 Its main objective is to upgrade member states' leather sectors through training, research and development, consultancy services and information dissemination. The COMESA/Leather and Leather Products Institute (LLPI) headquartered in Addis Ababa, Ethiopia, was established by the signing of the Charter by COMESA Member States in Mbabane, Swaziland on 23rd November 1990 in order to promote productivity, competitiveness, trade and regional integration in the leather sub-sector through the provision of the following key services: http://www.comesa-llpi.org/index.php/who-we-are rei120.17 rei120.17cs.txt

The objective of the Clearing House is to promote cooperation in the settlement of payments for intraPTA trade. 19920999 The PTA reinsurance company (ZEPRE): Established in September 1992, ZEPRE is headquartered in Nairobi, Kenya. Its function is to reduce the outflow of foreign exchange in the form of payments to overseas reinsurance companies by providing reinsurance services for companies within the PTA. http://www.zep-re.com/index.php?option=com_docman&task=doc_details&gid=2&Itemid=99 rei120.18 rei120.18cs.txt

\subsection*{ILP} 

Also in 2000, COMESA signed a Trade and Investment Framework Agreement (TIFA) with the United States Trade Representative that establishes a TIFA Council for a structured dialogue on trade and investment issues. 

\section*{Community of Sahel and Saharan States (CEN-SAD), rei140}

treaty list done 201211 by gary goertz 
treaty coding finished 201305 by gary goertz 

http://www.uneca.org/cen-sad/index.htm
201211 "site under construction" secretariat probably became completely disfunctional during civil war in libya

CEN-SAD was established on 4th February 1998 following the Conference of Leaders and Heads of States held in Tripoli (Great Jahamiriya). The Treaty on the establishment of the Community was signed by the Leader of Great El-Fateh Revolution and the Heads of State of Burkina Faso, Mali, Niger, Chad and Sudan. The Central African Republic and Eritrea joined the Community during the first Summit of the organization held in Syrte in April 1999. Senegal, Djibouti and Gambia joined during the N'djamena Summit in February 2000. Others countries joined later, and still more are in the process of joining the Organization.

It may be noted that CEN-SAD Community was recognized as a regional economic one during the thirty sixth ordinary session of the Conference of Leaders and Heads of State and Government of the Organization of African Unity held on 04-12/07/2000 in Lomé in Togo.

CEN-SAD institutions comprise the Conference of Heads of State and Government, which is the apex authority and convenes every year on a rotating and alternative basis in the different capitals of the member countries, the Executive Council grouping the ministers in charge of Foreign Affairs, Economy, Finance,Planning, Home Affairs and Security. 

Also, this regional entity has a secretariat based in Tripoli led by a secretary general in charge of monitoring the functioning of the different institutions and overseeing the application of the decisions and recommendations adopted by the Conference of Heads of States, and the objectives of the Constitutive Treaty.

Besides, the Community is endowed with a financial instrument -- CEN SAD Bank for Investment and Trade -- headquartered at Tripoli.

This institution is meant to finance development projects within the CEN-SAD sub-region and contribute to various banking, financial, commercial and investment activities in the member countries.

To prop up its social, economic and cultural policies, CEN-SAD has instituted a Bamako-based Social, Economic and Cultural Council grouping 5 representatives of each country and comprising the commission in charge of planning, economy and finance, one addressing education, cultural, sciences, information and rural development issues, and another commission in charge of transports, communications and energy.

The five organs of CEN-SAD are:

1. The Conference of the Heads of States

2. The Executive Council

3. The Secretariat General

4. The African Bank for Development and Trade

5. The Economic, Social and Cultural Council (ESCC)

19980214 -- Treaty founding CEN-SAD rei140.01 rei140.01cs.txt 

20040599 Organisation ferroviaire régionale de la CEN-SAD censad_sg@yahoo.com - info@cen-sad.org Founded May 2004, Tripoli (Libyan AJ). Comes within Community of Sahel-Saharan States rei140.02 rei140.02cs.txt

\section*{Union économique et monétaire ouest-africaine (UEMOA), rei360}

english name: West African Economic and Monetary Union

treaty list last checked 201211 
coding sheets checked by gary goertz 201311 

official web site: 
http://www.uemoa.int/Pages/Home.aspx
site give free trade agreements, decisions, etc.
http://www.ecowex.com/

note that the reglements are not directly accessible via the website, use devonagent with "reglement" AND "UEMOA"

this has apparently complete info on decisions, reglements, etc, but only starting 2001
http://www.izf.net/pages/bulletins-officiels-uemoa/2274/

UEMOA was created by a Treaty signed at Dakar, Senegal, on 10 January 1994, by the heads of state and governments of Benin, Burkina Faso, Côte d'Ivoire, Mali, Niger, Senegal, and Togo. On 2 May 1997, Guinea-Bissau, a former Portuguese colony, became the organization's eighth (and only non-Francophone) member state. Union douanière, entrée en vigueur le 1er janvier 2000

NOTE: we consider a few "reglements" as treaties if they are important. We exclude "decisions." "acte additionel" are generally considered treaties. 

see also West African Monetary Zone, ecowas countries trying to form common currency

\section*{PIF rei460, Pacific Islands Forum}

treaty list last checked 201209 by gary goertz 
coding sheets last checked 201209 by gary goertz 

note that there are regional environmental agreements that cover basically the same countries, but which are not formally part of the PIF, e.g., Protocol for the Prevention of Pollution of the South Pacific Region by Dumping, 1990, 1986 Convention on the Conservation of Nature in the South Pacific, "Noumea Convention", Agreement Establishing the South Pacific Regional Environment Programme (SPREP), 1993;

other names: Melanesian Spearhead Group Trade Agreement (MSG), South Pacific Forum, South Pacific Bureau for Economic Cooperation

``Forum Island Countries'' means the Cook Islands, Federated States of Micronesia, Fiji Islands, Kiribati, Republic of the Marshall Islands, Nauru, Niue, Republic of Palau, Papua New Guinea, Samoa, Solomon Islands, Tonga, Tuvalu and Vanuatu;

official web site with basically all documents: 
http://www.forumsec.org/

19659999 Pacific Islands Producers Association rei460.11
In 1965 Fiji and Western Samoa set up the Pacific Islands Producers' Association (PIPA) to promote closer co-operation between the Islands supplying bananas to New Zealand. Tonga, the cook Islands, Niue and later Kiribati and Tuvalu joined. PIPA gradually broadened its activities to include production and marketing in other industries and became involved in political questions. In 1971 it asked New Zealand to host a meeting of heads of government of common interest. Out of this exploratory meeting the south Pacific Forum was born. Early meetings in the 1970s focused on regional trade and economic issues; later meetings on transport and shipping. To facilitate its work the Forum established the South Pacific bureau of Economic Co-operation in Suva with which PIPA merged. In 1977 ten forum countries started a joint shipping venture, the Pacific forum Line. To develop a fishing industry in the two hundred mile exclusive economic zones they set up a Forum fisheries Agency in 1979. duty-free access on a non-reciprocal basis to New Zealand and Australian markets for almost all products by Forum countries was permitted under the South Pacific Regional Trade and Economic Cooperation Agreement (SPARTECA) OF 1980. we consider this a precursor and not a treaty of PIF

19679999 Another regional institution which was oriented towards meeting the needs and problems of new island states was the University of the south Pacific (USP), set up up on an old flying base site gifted by New Zealand at Lancala Bay, Suva in 1967

19730417 Agreement establishing the South Pacific Bureau for economic co-operation (with annex)Notes and references Signed definitively for Australia 17 April 1973. ATS 1973 No. 0013 ; NZTS 1973 No. 18; UNTS 874 p. 163. See also Amendments of 31 August 1977 and 20 September 1978 (below). Terminated 23 April 1993 by Agreement of 29 July 1991 rei460.12 rei460.12tt1.txt rei460.12cs.txt

It allows duty free access for the products of Forum Island Countries (FICs) to the markets of Australia and New Zealand, subject to "Rules of Origin" regulations. see reidevon "not a treaty" because it is a hub and spoke agreement rei460.05 not a treaty rei460.05tt1.txt

20070128 DRAFT PROTOCOL ON THE ESTABLISHMENT OF THE EASTERN AFRICA STANDBY BRIGADE (EASBRIG) rei475.03 rei475.03tt1.pdf EASBRICOM was operationalized following the approval by the 1st Extraordinary Summit of Head of State and Government of the Eastern Africa Region, held on the 28thJanuary 2007 http://www.easbrig.org/ (does not seem to work) During the meeting it was observed that the 13 EASBRIG member states are also members of several regional economic blocs, namely, COMESA, the East African Community (EAC), IGAD and the Southern Africa Development Community (SADC). This creates interfaces since no single regional economic community (REC) accommodates all 13 member states; the difficulty, however, is in designating one single REC to manage the EASBRIG.6 None of the existing RECs could therefore claim to represent completely EASBRIG on behalf of the AU, while recognising the designated interim role allocated to IGAD in this respect. The EACDS therefore decided that the appropriate role of IGAD would be that of interim coordination, including coordination of all activities of the EASBRIG, calling meetings of the Council of Ministers of Defence and Security for EASBRIG and the East African Ministers of Defence and Security, undertaking fundraising in conjunction with other RECs, the AU and the UN to support the work of EASBRIG, providing and sharing information to facilitate planning for the EASBRIG and establishing an EASBRIG fund to coordinate donor funding and resources offered by the international community.

\section*{CARICOM, Caribbean Common Market, rei520}

official web site: http://www.caricom.org when checking for new documents, check "treaties" "agreements" etc.

coding sheets checked 201207 by gary goertz 

we consider caricom to have started with the creation of carifta in 1966

annual meetings have "commumiques" which can provide a lot of information. site search engine does not work well, just use google with caricom as part of search

treaties and protocols are located in the web site under "information services" http://www.caricom.org/expframes2.htm

-check about carifta and process of signing, case of guyana and its exceptions In 1972, Commonwealth Caribbean leaders at the Seventh Heads of Government Conference decided to transform the Caribbean Free Trade Association (CARIFTA) into a Common Market and establish the Caribbean Community, of which the Common Market would be an integral part.

The signing of the Treaty establishing the Caribbean Community, Chaguaramas, 4th July 1973, was a defining moment in the history of the Commonwealth Caribbean. Although a free-trade area had been established, CARIFTA did not provide for the free movement of labour and capital, or the coordination of agricultural, industrial and foreign policies.

annual meetings have "commumiques" which can provide a lot of information site search engine does not work well, just use google with caricom as part of search

treaties and protocols are located in the web site under "information services" http://www.caricom.org/expframes2.htm

-check about carifta and process of signing, case of guyana and its exceptions In 1972, Commonwealth Caribbean leaders at the Seventh Heads of Government Conference decided to transform the Caribbean Free Trade Association (CARIFTA) into a Common Market and establish the Caribbean Community, of which the Common Market would be an integral part.

The signing of the Treaty establishing the Caribbean Community, Chaguaramas, 4th July 1973, was a defining moment in the history of the Commonwealth Caribbean. Although a free-trade area had been established, CARIFTA did not provide for the free movement of labour and capital, or the coordination of agricultural, industrial and foreign policies.

19980000 Memorandum of Understanding on the Establishment and Operation of an Association of Civil Aviation Authorities of the Caribbean Need to find signing dates at least, With regard to the regulatory environment, Member States have finalized after a period of national and regional consultations a Multilateral Agreement Concerning the Operation of Air Services Within the Caribbean Community, commonly called the CARICOM Multilateral Air Services Agreement (MASA), which, as at 11 July 2000, has been signed by all Member States except The Bahamas, Jamaica and Montserrat. Eight of these States have also ratified. The Agreement entered into force in November 1998. It marks an imporeint step towards the establishment of a Single Market for air transport services as it provides the formal framework for the provision of air services between the States party to the Agreement by the air carriers of those States. not a treaty rei520.57 rei520.57tt1.txt rei520.57cs.txt

http://diplomatie.belgium.be/fr/documentation/

3 Feb 1958, The Hague (Netherlands), on signature of the Treaty of Union by representatives of Belgium, Luxembourg (Luxembourg), Netherlands; Treaty came into force 1 Nov 1960. Belgium and the Grand Duchy of Luxembourg had been linked, since 1921, by the Belgian-Luxembourg Economic Union, which still exists within the Benelux Union. The political initiative to bring together the economies of the Netherlands, Belgium and Luxembourg, taken during World War II, and which eventually led to the economic integration of these countries, had been started with the adoption of a Monetary Agreement, 21 Oct 1943, London (UK), a Customs Union Treaty, 5 Sep 1944, London, and the setting up of Benelux Customs Union, 1 Jan 1948. Renewed Benelux Treaty, signed 17 June 2008, The Hague (Netherlands). Statutes registered in UNTS 1/11096

we consider that the BEU starts in 1948

we only consider "conventions" as treaty for the REI project

1. le Comit de Ministres peut prendre des dcisions portant excution des dispositions du Trait Benelux dans le respect des conditions du Trait. Ces dcisions engagent les Etats membres. Pour tre galement contraignantes l'gard des citoyens des trois pays du Benelux, les dcisions doivent tre transposes en rglementation nationale; 2. le Comit de Ministres peut tablir des conventions, qui seront ensuite soumises aux trois Etats membres. Les conventions sont des engagements juridiquement contraignants entre les trois Etats membres du Benelux. Ces conventions sont mises en vigueur conformment aux dispositions constitutionnelles de chacun des Etats membres; 3. le Comit de Ministres peut faire des recommandations pour les besoins du fonctionnement du Benelux. Ces recommandations n'ont pas de force juridiquement contraignante, mais elles imposent une certaine obligation morale aux Etats membres de conformer leur lgislation la recommandation; 4. le Comit de Ministres peut donner des directives au Conseil Benelux et au Secrtariat gnral. Ces directives sont contraignantes pour les instances auxquelles elles s'adressent.

\section*{European Free Trade Agreement (EFTA), rei600}

http://www.efta.int/

treaty list last checked 201210
coding sheets last checked 201210

see foreign treaties, the english version is in the file with norwegian translation.
Norway: http://www.lovdata.no/traktater/index.html

The founding members of EFTA were Austria, Denmark, Norway, Portugal, Sweden, Switzerland and the United Kingdom. Finland became an associate member in 1961 (becoming a full member in 1986) and Iceland joined in 1970. The United Kingdom and Denmark joined the European Communities in 1973 (together with Ireland), and hence ceased to be EFTA members. Portugal also left the EFTA for the European Community in 1986. Liechtenstein joined in 1991 (previously its interests in EFTA had been represented by Switzerland). Finally, Austria, Sweden and Finland joined the European Union in 1995 and thus ceased to be EFTA members.

The EEA Agreement, an international treaty, was signed on 2 May 1992 between the European Community and the EU Member States, and the three EFTA States Iceland, Norway and Liechtenstein.

NOTE: EFTA has a system whereby "decisions" made by the Council are legally binding and then incorporated into the EFTA treaty. As such we include these decisions as functioning as the equivalent to amendments to the treaty. This results, however, in a many small documents.

\section*{Nordic Council, NC, rei630} 

treaty list last checked 201301
coding sheets last checked 201301 by gary goertz 

http://www.norden.org/

this website could work if one knew norwegian
Norway: http://www.lovdata.no/traktater/index.html

in norwegian "Nordisk Rad"

United Nations treaty series?

We consider the Nordic Council to begin with the Helsinki Treaty in 1962. The nordic council considers the "constitutional" document.

1952, by Statute drawn up by governments of Denmark, Iceland, Norway and Sweden. Finland adhered in 1955. Since 1970 the autonomous territories of the Faeroes and the Aland Islands have their own representatives on the Council and, since 1984, Greenland is also represented. The Council is sometimes referred to in English as Nordic Council of Parliamentarians (NCP). It was based in Stockholm (Sweden) until Aug 1996, when it moved to Copenhagen (Denmark), where it is housed with the Secretariat of the Nordic Council of Ministers

\section*{Eurasian Economic Community, EAEC-EurAsEC, rei670}

The Constitutive Treaty of the EuroAsian Economic Community was signed on October 10, 2000 in the capital of Kazakhstan, Astana, by Presidents of Belarus, Kazakhstan, Kyrgyz Republic, Russia and Tajikistan. In May, 2002 on the governments' request Moldova and Ukraine have got the status of observers in EurAsEC. On October 6, 2005, at the Summit of the "Central Asian Cooperation Organization (CACO)" the decision on joining the CACO with the EurAsEC initiated by the president of Uzbekistan was made by the heads of the member states of CACO in order to facilitate economic integration and development in Eurasia.

\section*{Central Asian Cooperation Organization, CACO, rei680}

no website, 

coding considered done in the absence of any treaties gary goertz 201010

ceased to exist in 2005 because it was absorbed in eurasian economic union

see also:
http://ecetrade.typepad.com/rtas/guam_rtg/

The Central Asian Cooperation Organization was initially created under the name of Central Asian Economic Union in 1994, by Kazakhstan, Kyrgyzstan and Uzbekistan. Tajikistan joined the group in 1998, and the Organization was then renamed Central Asian Economic Cooperation (CAEC). On February 28th, 2002, the CAEC was transformed into the Central Asian Cooperation Organization, (CACO). On May 28th, 2004, Russia joined CACO as a member.

The Central Asian Cooperation Organization and the Euroasian Economic Community are merging; this was announced during the meeting of the CACO council in St. Petersburg. The Chairman of CACO, President of Tajikistan Emomali Rakhmonov, presented the decision by the heads of governments on October 6, 2005 at the press conference. Aleksandr Lukashenko, the president of Belarus - which is the only country within EEC and not a member of CACO - mentioned that he doesn't mind if these two organizations merge.

Member States: Kazakhstan, Kyrgyzstan, Russia (since May 28th, 2004), Tajikistan and Uzbekistan.

Observers: Georgia, Turkey and Ukraine

no treaties seem to be available online

19940000 rei680.01 rei680.01cs.txt Central Asian Economic Union created

19980000 rei680.02 renamed Central Asian Economic Cooperation (CAEC), Tajikistan joins

20020228 rei680.03 CAEC was transformed into the Central Asian Cooperation Organization, (CACO)

2005000 fusion with EAEC, hence organization no longer exists 

\section*{Shanghai Cooperation Organization, SCO, rei685}

http://www.sectsco.org/EN/

also known as Shanghai Five

The Shanghai Five grouping was originally created 26 April, 1996 with the signing of the Treaty on Deepening Military Trust in Border Regions in Shanghai by the heads of states of Kazakhstan, the People's Republic of China, Kyrgyzstan, Russia and Tajikistan. 24 April, 1997 the same countries signed the Treaty on Reduction of Military Forces in Border Regions in a meeting in Moscow.

Republic of Kazakhstan, the People's Republic of China, the Kyrgyz Republic, the Russian Federation, the Republic of Tajikistan and the Republic of Uzbekistan

20010000 rei685.0001cs.txt ``The Shanghai Convention on Combating Terrorism, Separatism, and Extremism'' rei685.0001tt.txt 

20010615 "Declaration on Establishment of Shanghai Cooperation Organization" at a meeting in Shanghai, "cradle" of the mechanism, Heads of "Shanghai five" member-states and President of the Republic of Uzbekistan unanimously decided to lift the mechanism of "Shanghai Five" to a higher level, in order to make it strong base and important support for developing under new conditions cooperation among six states. To these purposes Heads of six states signed the Declaration on Establishment of the Shanghai Cooperation Organisation, declared a birth of the new organisation of regional cooperation SCO. During the meeting "the Shanghai convention on fight against terrorism, separatism and extremism" was also signed. It happened three months prior to the tragedy of September 11, 2001. Thus, the SCO has become the pioneer organization, which has precisely proposed fighting against terrorism on the international level. http://www.sectsco.org/news_detail.asp?id=88&LanguageID=2 rei685.01 rei685.01tt1.txt Declaration, not a treaty

\section*{Economic Cooperation Organization (ECO), rei860}

treaty list last revised by goertz 201010
treaties coded by goertz 201010

http://www.ecosecretariat.org/

for documents see:
http://www.ecosecretariat.org/MainMenu/Documents.htm#_jmp0_

see also
http://ecetrade.typepad.com/rtas/eco_rtg/

Member States: Afghanistan, Azerbaijan, Iran, Pakistan, Kazakhstan, Kyrgyzstan, Tajikistan, Turkey, Turkmenistan, and Uzbekistan 

ECO is the successor organization of Regional Cooperation for Development (RCD) which remained in existence since 1964 up to 1979.

Economic Cooperation Organization (ECO), is an intergovernmental regional organization established in 1985 by Iran, Pakistan and Turkey for the purpose of promoting economic, technical and cultural cooperation among the Member States.

In 1992, the Organization was expanded to include seven new members, namely: Islamic Republic of Afghanistan, Republic of Azerbaijan, Republic of Kazakhstan, Kyrgyz Republic, Republic of Tajikistan, Turkmenistan and Republic of Uzbekistan. The date of the Organization's expansion to its present strength, 28th November, is being observed as the ECO Day.
